Meeting Minutes / Correspondence
                        Memorandum of Meeting

To:                   File

From:                 Bernie Boerchers, Keller and Kirkpatrick

Date:                 February 26, 2007

Project Name:         Maplewood Township Traffic Calming
                      Township of Maplewood, Essex County

Project Number:       2006669.00

Subject:              Field Meeting

Copy:                 Attendees




A field meeting was conducted for the above referenced project at 10:00 A.M. on Thursday,
February 22, 2007. Those in attendance were as follows:

Attendee              Bureau / Company                                         Phone
Richard Calbi         Maplewood Township Engineer                              973 762-8120
Matthew Cho           Maplewood Township Engineer's Office                     973 762-8120
Bernie Boerchers      Keller and Kirkpatrick (K&K)                             908 236-9001
Julia Steponanko      K&K                                                      908 236-9001

The purpose of the meeting was to verify the problem statement, review the existing conditions
and discuss conceptual traffic calming solutions at the following locations:

¾ Intersections:
  · Parker Avenue and Valley Street
  · Jefferson Avenue and Maplewood Avenue
  · Jefferson Avenue and Woodland / Walton Roads
  · Elmwood Avenue and Prospect Street
  · Jefferson Avenue and Valley Street
  · Cedar Lane and Ridgewood Road

¾ Roadways:
  · Ridgewood Road
  · Boyden Avenue
  · Prospect Street
  · Parker Avenue
   ·   Baker Street
   ·   Jacoby Street

¾ Other Locations:
  · Sommer Avenue including Hubert Place, Osborne Terrace, and Girard Place
  · Kensington Terrace

The following items were discussed at each location:

¾ Parker Avenue and Valley Street

   1. The problem statement for this signalized intersection identifies capacity issues
      during peak commuting hours and school time periods of entry and dismissal. It also
      recommends the investigation of pedestrian safety enhancements with respect to the
      significant pedestrian activity, specifically schoolchildren from Columbia High School
      located in the northeast quadrant of the intersection.

   2. Mr. Boerchers stated that based on the recently collected traffic count data and the
      existing timing directive that the intersection operates at an acceptable Level of
      Service (LOS) during each of the peak hours. However, the attendees did observe
      vehicles traveling either north or south along Valley Street passing left turning
      vehicles on the right thereby creating a "shadowing effect".

   3. Mr. Calbi recommended the installation of bump-outs to narrow the travel lanes along
      Valley Street and Parker Avenue to reduce the potential for motorists passing left
      turning vehicles on the right and thereby reduce the number of sideswipe crashes. It
      was added that the bump-outs would reduce pedestrian crossing times.

   4. Mr. Boerchers recommended replacing the existing traffic signal trombone mast arms
      and eight-inch signal heads with standard traffic signal mast arms and twelve-inch
      signal heads to increase signal visibility and thereby reduce the number of rear end
      crashes.

   5. The attendees observed that some of the existing pedestrian signal heads were not
      functioning and that others had poor visibility. In addition, it was noted that
      pedestrian signal heads were not present in the northeast quadrant of the
      intersection. Mr. Boerchers recommended the installation of countdown pedestrian
      signals in the northeast quadrant and the replacement of all of the existing pedestrian
      signal heads with countdown pedestrian signal heads to increase pedestrian
      awareness.

   6. The attendees agreed that additional "No Right Turn on Red" signs should be added
      at the appropriate locations to supplement existing signing.

   7. It was suggested that an exclusive left turn lane be added along the westbound
      approach of Parker Avenue due to the significant left turn volume along this
      approach. Mr. Boerchers stated that the addition of an exclusive left turn lane along
      this approach would require widening along the eastbound approach along which
      there are physical constraints preventing such a widening. He added that the



                                                                                            2
     addition of an exclusive left turn lane would also increase the pedestrian crossing
     time and that the intersection currently operates at an acceptable LOS.

  8. Mr. Cabli noted that the County would be responsible for the proposed improvements
     at this intersection.

  9. Subsequent to the meeting it was observed that pedestrians cross at the unsignalized
     intersection of Valley Street and Cromwell Place, which is located approximately 420
     feet to the south of the signalized intersection of Valley Street and Parker Avenue.
     While pedestrian handicaps exist at the intersection of Valley Street and Cromwell
     Place, there are no marked crosswalks.

¾ Jefferson Avenue and Maplewood Avenue

  1. The problem statement for the intersection of Jefferson Avenue and Maplewood
     Avenue identifies limited intersection sight distance along with a steep grade and
     speeding along Jefferson Avenue as the causes of a significant number of crashes.
     The intersection is currently controlled by stop signs along the Maplewood Avenue
     approaches. In addition, a flashing signal and approach warning signs exist to warn
     motorists of the hazardous intersection.

  2. It was noted that the existing profile along Jefferson Avenue west of Maplewood
     Avenue is substandard and severely limits both stopping sight distance along
     Jefferson Avenue and intersection sight distance from both approaches of
     Maplewood Avenue. It was also noted that intersection sight distance is restricted by
     existing vegetation and grading. Mr. Calbi stated that the Township has an ordinance
     restricting obstructions/vegetation within the sight triangles at intersections and that
     he would provide K&K with a copy of the ordinance. The attendees agreed that the
     sight triangles should be cleared of all obstructions.

  3. It was noted that the existing pavement markings were in poor condition.

  4. Motorists were observed speeding along Jefferson Avenue.

  5. It was noted that a previous suggestion to address crashes at this intersection was
     the installation of a four-way stop condition. It was agreed by the attendees that the
     installation of stop signs along Jefferson Avenue would most likely increase the
     number of rear end crashes along Jefferson Avenue due to the substandard profile.

  6. Mr. Boerchers stated that one possible solution to address right angle crashes at this
     intersection would be the installation of a roundabout. He added that a roundabout
     may also increase rear end crashes along Jefferson Avenue, but that the delay would
     most likely be less than that of a four-way stop and therefore the frequency of rear
     end crashes should be less. He noted that the apron, while being distinct, would
     most likely have to be a traversable surface to accommodate larger vehicles that may
     be traveling to and from Maplewood Village along Maplewood Avenue.

  7. The attendees agreed that the roadway width for Jefferson Avenue, especially west
     of Maplewood Avenue, should be reduced to discourage speeding. Options that



                                                                                            3
      were discussed for narrowing Jefferson Avenue included the installation of a sidewalk
      along the eastbound direction, striping for a bicycle lane and/or parking, and/or bump-
      outs at the corners of the intersection. It was noted that the demand may not exist for
      on-street parking and thereby reduce its' effectiveness as a traffic calming measure.

   8. The attendees discussed the possibility of bringing the substandard profile along
      Jefferson Avenue into conformance with current standards. This would significantly
      improve both stopping and intersection sight distance at this location. It was agreed
      that such a modification would significantly impact adjoining properties and require
      the reconstruction of existing retaining walls and driveways. It would also impact
      existing utilities. Mr. Boerchers stated that a detour would most likely be required to
      reduce the grade along Jefferson Avenue. He added that K&K would survey the
      existing profile along Jefferson Avenue and develop a limited number of critical cross
      sections to determine the feasibility of reducing the grade along Jefferson Avenue.

   9. Mr. Calbi stated that the Maplewood Township Police would perform a speed study
      along Jefferson Avenue prior to any improvements so that a before and after analysis
      could be performed to determine the effectiveness of those improvements.

¾ Jefferson Avenue and Woodland / Walton Roads

   1. The problem statement for the intersection of Jefferson Avenue and Woodland /
      Walton Roads identifies limited intersection sight distance and speeding along the
      approach roadways. The intersection is currently controlled by stop signs along
      Woodland Road and Walton Road, which are offset. This intersection is located
      approximately 420 feet west of the intersection of Jefferson Avenue and Maplewood
      Avenue.

   2. It was observed by the attendees that intersection sight distance is restricted by
      existing vegetation and grading within the sight triangles. The attendees agreed that
      the sight triangles should be cleared of all obstructions.

   3. As noted at the previous location, the existing profile along Jefferson Avenue, in this
      case east of Woodland / Walton Roads, is substandard and severely limits both
      stopping sight distance along Jefferson Avenue and intersection sight distance from
      Woodland / Walton Roads. See previous location for discussion regarding a possible
      modification to the existing profile along Jefferson Avenue.

   4. It was noted that pavement markings, including stop lines, do not exist along each of
      the approach roadways and that the appropriate striping should be installed as a
      minimum. It was also recommended that a crosswalk be installed along the
      eastbound approach of Jefferson Avenue and that signing to direct pedestrians to this
      crosswalk be added in the appropriate corners of the intersection.

   5. As at the previous location, the attendees agreed that the roadway width for Jefferson
      Avenue should be reduced to discourage speeding and recommended options similar
      to those recommended at the previous location.

   6. Mr. Calbi stated that a crash involving a Maplewood Township police vehicle recently



                                                                                            4
      occurred at this intersection and that a consultant performed a thorough investigation
      of the crash. He added that his office would provide K&K with a copy of the
      consultant's report summarizing the investigation and its conclusions.

¾ Elmwood Avenue and Prospect Street

   1. The problem statement for the intersection of Elmwood Avenue and Prospect Street
      identifies turning difficulties from Elmwood Avenue, which forms the stem of this `T'
      intersection, onto Prospect Street along with speeding along Prospect Street. In
      addition, significant pedestrian activity has been identified with the crosswalks at this
      intersection. The intersection is controlled by a stop sign located along Elmwood
      Avenue.

   2. The attendees observed that intersection sight distance from Elmwood Avenue is
      obstructed by vegetation located within the sight triangles and the profile of Prospect
      Avenue south of Elmwood Avenue. The attendees agreed that the sight triangles
      should be cleared of all obstructions.

   3. To enhance pedestrian safety, it was recommended that "ladder" striping be added to
      the crosswalks to increase their visibility, additional warning signs be installed along
      the approach roadways to provide advance warning to motorists and that bump-outs
      be provided to reduce pedestrian crossing times and narrow the roadway width of
      Prospect Avenue in an attempt to reduce speeds along the same.

¾ Jefferson Avenue and Valley Street

   1. The problem statement for the intersection of Jefferson Avenue and Valley Street
      identifies limited intersection sight distance along with a steep grade along Jefferson
      Avenue, which forms the stem of this `T' intersection, as hazards at this intersection
      to both motorists and pedestrians.

   2. Mr. Boerchers stated that based on the recently collected traffic volumes and crash
      data that a traffic signal is not warranted at this intersection.

   3. It was noted that the intersection sight distance from Jefferson Avenue was limited
      due to parking on Valley Street and existing vegetation. The attendees agreed that
      the sight triangles should be cleared of all obstructions. K&K will overlay the required
      sight triangles onto an aerial of the intersection to determine the limits of no parking
      along Valley Street so as not to obstruct intersection sight distance from Jefferson
      Avenue. Mr. Boerchers recommended the installation of bump-outs in both the
      southwest and northwest corners of the intersection to reduce pedestrian crossing
      times and allow for the relocation of the stop line along Jefferson Avenue further to
      the east thereby increasing intersection sight distance.

   4. Mr. Calbi suggested that the existing near side NJ Transit bus stop located along
      Valley Street southbound, north of Jefferson Avenue, be relocated south of Jefferson
      Avenue as a far side bus stop. It was noted that this would require the elimination of
      existing on street parking along Valley Street in front of local businesses. It was
      added, however, that these businesses have off street parking behind their buildings.



                                                                                             5
   5. It was observed that the existing centerline striping along Jefferson Avenue was in
      poor condition and requires maintenance.

   6. It was observed that the street name signing for Jefferson Avenue was obscure. It
      was recommended that either the street name signing be enhanced or that advanced
      warning signs for Jefferson Avenue be installed along Valley Street.

   7. It was agreed by the attendees that the implementation of additional pedestrian safety
      measures need to be investigated including modified crosswalks and signing for
      enhanced visibility and advanced warning for motorists.

¾ Cedar Lane and Ridgewood Road

   1. The problem statement for the intersection of Cedar Lane and Ridgewood Road
      identifies limited intersection sight distance as a hazard at this intersection. The
      intersection is currently controlled by stop signs located along Cedar Lane. Buildings
      are located within three of the four sight triangles.

   2. Mr. Boerchers stated that based on the recently collected traffic volumes and crash
      data that a four-way stop is not warranted at this intersection.

   3. The attendees observed that in addition to the existing buildings, illegally parked
      vehicles along Ridgewood Road northbound, north of Cedar Lane, were limiting the
      available intersection sight distance from Cedar Lane. It was suggested that yellow
      striping be installed in the areas of no parking. Subsequent to the meeting bump-outs
      and the widening of the existing sidewalk in front of the local businesses located
      along Ridgewood Road northbound, north of Cedar Lane, were also discussed as
      viable options.

¾ Ridgewood Road / Boyden Avenue / Prospect Street

   1. The problem statements for Ridgewood Road, Boyden Avenue and Prospect Street
      identify speeding as the main hazard along these roadways. In addition, difficult turn
      maneuvers from intersecting streets were identified as a hazard along Ridgewood
      Road.

   2. The attendees discussed such options as the addition of parking and/or bike lanes,
      bump-outs and roundabouts to narrow the travel way along these roadways and thus
      reduce the travel speed. It was also suggested that a raised median could be
      installed along Prospect Street to provide a boulevard effect, which would reduce the
      travel speed and allow for a pedestrian refuge in the middle of the roadway.

   3. It was recommended that extension track striping be installed at the intersection of
      Boyden Avenue and Elmwood Avenue to direct motorists through the intersection.




                                                                                           6
¾ Parker Avenue and Kensington Terrace

   1. The intersection of Parker Avenue and Kensington Terrace along with the intersection
      of Parker Avenue and Valley Street, which is located approximately 400 feet to the
      west, are immediately adjacent to Columbia High School thereby experiencing
      significant pedestrian traffic and have also been identified in the their respective
      problem statements as being congested.

   2. It was recommended that bump-outs be considered at the intersection of Parker
      Avenue and Kensington Terrace to reduce pedestrian crossing times and narrow the
      roadway.

¾ Baker Street

   1. The problem statement for Baker Street identifies speeding and limited visibility,
      resulting from the underpass, combined with heavy pedestrian traffic as hazards
      along this roadway between Maplewood Avenue and Valley Street.

   2. It was stated that the crosswalks across Baker Street between Dunnell Road and
      Burnett Street are in poor condition and that "ladder" striping, advance warning signs,
      bump-outs and/or raised crosswalks should be considered to enhance pedestrian
      safety and increase driver awareness of these pedestrian crossings.

   3. It was noted that the intersection of Baker Street and Maplewood Avenue is confusing
      to motorists and that additional signing and striping should be investigated to increase
      driver expectancy.

¾ Jacoby Street

   1. The problem statement notes that some motorists utilize Jacoby Street as a bypass
      between Springfield Avenue and Boyden Avenue. Speeding and limited sight
      distance has also been noted along Jacoby Street.

   2. Mr. Calbi stated that 44th Street is also used as a bypass route to get to Chancellor
      Avenue.

   3. It was suggested that 44th Street could be made a one-way street towards Chancellor
      Avenue or that a gate could be constructed across 44th Street and its intersection with
      Chancellor Avenue, essentially making 44th Street a dead end.

   4. It was suggested to make Jacoby Street a right-in, right-out only by constructing a
      divisional island along Springfield Avenue.

¾ Sommer Avenue including Hubert Place, Osborne Terrace and Girard Place

   1. The problem statement notes that this collection of roadways are used by motorists
      as a bypass between Valley Street and Prospect Street / Springfield Avenue and that
      speeding also occurs along these roadways.



                                                                                             7
    2. It was suggested to create a one-way street grid in this area to discourage the use of
       these roadways as bypass routes. It was also suggested to install speed tables along
       Sommer Avenue.

    3. It was agreed by the attendees that bump-outs and roundabouts should be
       investigated to reduce speed along these roadways and discourage their use as
       bypass routes.

¾ Kensington Terrace

    1. The problem statement notes that Kensington Terrace is used as a bypass for Valley
       Street and that speeding frequently occurs along Kensington Terrace.

    2. It was suggested to allow school parking along Kensington Terrace to narrow the
       travel lanes and thereby discourage the use of Kensington Terrace as a bypass
       route. It was stated that residents do not want parking along this street due to
       students loitering in the area.

    3. It was suggested to install bump-outs or speed tables along Kensington Terrace
       and/or install a roundabout at the intersection of Kensington Terrace and Edgewood
       Road to reduce the frequency of speeding and discourage the use of Kensington
       Terrace as a bypass route.

Action Items:

    ·    K&K will prepare preliminary plans indicating the conceptual solutions as discussed at this
         meeting.

    ·    The Maplewood Township Engineer's office will provide K&K with a copy of the report
         regarding the crash involving a police vehicle at the intersection of Jefferson Avenue and
         Woodland / Walton Roads.

    ·    Maplewood Township Police will perform a speed study along Jefferson Avenue.


This memorandum of record is believed to be an accurate record of the discussions at this meeting. If any of the
attendees disagree with the documented discussion, please contact Bernie Boerchers at (908) 236-9001 within 5 days of
receipt of minutes. If no comments are received, then this memorandum will be considered a true and accurate record of
this meeting.

7/23/2007
                   MAPLEWOOD TRAFFIC SURVEY SUMMARY

Intersections Identified To Be Problematic (# of complaints)

1. Parker & Valley (17) - This area has been identified most frequently in the survey as
a bottleneck area during rush hours and before and after school. There are many
pedestrians in the area when school is over and the crosswalks across both streets become
very busy and pose hazards to pedestrians, especially after school.
Crash Data: 20 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

2. Boyden Ave & Springfield Ave (12) - There were numerous complaints about the
timing of the signals and the constant bottleneck during peak hours on mostly Boyden
Ave in front of the Maplewood Pool and secondly Springfield Ave.
Crash Data: 32 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

3. Baker St. & Maplewood Ave (11) - Baker St and Maplewood Ave intersection is a
difficult intersection to maneuver because of the geometry. Many residents requested
additional signs or an intersection signal be installed in this intersection. There are a lot
of pedestrians in the area and vehicle traffic which make it even more difficult. This
intersection needs to be studied further.
Crash Data: 8 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

4. Jefferson & Maplewood (11) - This intersection has been identified for numerous
deficiencies. For those who turn on to Jefferson from Maplewood, it poses a turning
hazard with limited visibility from Maplewood Ave and speeding vehicles on Jefferson.
Crash Data: 34 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

5. Jefferson & Woodland/Walton (6) ­ This intersection is adjacent to Jefferson &
Maplewood intersection and experiences similar issues with turning visibility from
Woodland and Walton going on to Jefferson and speeding issues on Jefferson. Speeding
has been noted on both Woodland and Walton streets.
Crash Data: 5 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

6. Boyden Ave & Elmwood (6) - This area has been identified as an intersection where
drivers speed on both streets as they enter the intersection. This has been identified as an
accident hazard area and a pedestrian hazard area. Also the signal timing has been
questioned.
Crash Data: 20 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

7. Elmwood & Prospect (5) - This T-intersection has been identified to be a hazardous
turn area when a left and right turn is made from Elmwood to Prospect. Cars on
Prospect speed and it is difficult for drivers who are turning from Elmwood to see them.
Additionally it has been identified as a pedestrian hazard crossing on Elmwood and
Prospect.
Crash Data: 9 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004
8. Jefferson & Valley (5) - This T-intersection has been identified to be a visibility
hazard when a right and left turn is made from Jefferson to Valley St with the left turn
being especially difficult. There is an incline going on to Valley from Jefferson which
makes the turn more difficult. Additionally, pedestrians crossing Jefferson walking on
Valley are at risk from cars pulling too far to turn on to Valley from Jefferson.
Crash Data: 13 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

9. Cedar Lane and Ridgewood (4) - This four-way intersection has been noted due to a
hazardous turn area when making a left or right turn from Cedar Lane to Ridgewood Ave,
especially going downhill on Cedar Lane. There is speeding on Ridgewood and the
turning visibility is poor. Additionally there are pedestrians and joggers on Ridgewood
Ave that pose a hazard for cars making this turn.
Crash Data: 2 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

10. Tuscan Road and Valley St. (4) - This T-intersection has been identified to be a
hazardous turn area when a left and right turn is made from Tuscan to Valley. This area
is not signalized and there is pedestrian traffic on Valley, especially for the elementary
schools and commuters walking to the train station. This turn poses a hazard to both
pedestrians and cars turning on to Valley.
Crash Data: 11 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004


Roads Identified to be Problematic (# of complaints)

1. Ridgewood (14) ­ This road has been unanimously identified as a speeding area.
There is a good amount of pedestrian traffic and cars turning on to Ridgewood from the
intersecting streets make hazardous turns due to grade, visibility and speed of traffic.
Crash Data: 27 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

2. Boyden Ave (9) - Speeding was the greatest complaint on Boyden Ave along with
congestion on Springfield Ave intersection.
Crash Data: 168 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

3. Springfield (9) - Congestion throughout the street during rush hour and bottleneck at
Boyden Ave
Crash Data: 527 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

4. Maplewood Ave (7) ­ Bottleneck and pedestrian hazards identified
Crash Data: 85 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

5. Orchard Ave (5) - Speeding
Crash Data: 19 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

6. Prospect (5) ­ Speeding has been unanimously identified.
Crash Data: 78 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004
7. Valley St (5) ­ Congestion near Parker and Baker street during end of school has been
observed during rush hour. It has also been identified for being a speeding area
Crash Data: 266 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

8. Parker Ave (5) ­ Along with Valley Street, this area has been identified as a
congestion area, particularly near Columbia High School. Double parking is common
during school drop off and pick up hours and this enhances the congestion in the area.
Crash Data: 108 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

9. Baker St (4) ­ Speeding and visibility problems noted from the underpass, to
Memorial Library and Maplewood Middle School area to Valley Street. There is very
heavy pedestrian traffic on Baker throughout the day.
Crash Data: 50 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

10. Durand Rd (4) - Durand has been identified as a major thoroughfare for traffic
moving from Maplewood Ave to Ridgewood Rd and Wyoming Ave and vice versa.
Speeding has been the biggest complaint.
Crash Data: 8 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

11. Jacoby St (3) ­ Traffic trying to by pass Springfield and get on Boyden Ave
frequently use Jacoby St. Speeding has been unanimously observed, especially on a
curve behind Seth Boyden School where there is heavy pedestrian traffic and visibility is
limited.
Crash Data: 34 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

12. Tuscan Road (3) ­ Traffic and pedestrian hazards. Increase signage and more law
enforcement.
Crash Data: 29 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004


Other Areas of Note

1. Sommer/Girard/Harvard/Osborne (6) ­ This collection of streets has been
identified to be a speeding area because it is frequently used as a traversing route from
Valley to Prospect/Springfield and vice versa.
Crash Data: 24 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004
6-Sommer, 2-Girard, 14-Harvard, 2-Osborne

2. Garfield Place, Union Ave, Hudson Ave and Coolidge Rd - This street has been
observed to be used frequently by drivers who by pass the Irvington Ave and Boyden
Ave intersection traffic light trying to get to Irvington Ave from Boyden Ave and vice
versa. Temporary speed humps have been installed to mitigate the problem but issue
should be resolved for traffic moving from Irvington Ave to Boyden Ave.
Crash Data: 21 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004
4-Garfield, 10-Union, 4-Hudson, 3-Coolidge
3. Kensington Terrace (collective complaint from neighborhood association) ­
Traffic from Parker Ave, Oakland Road and Edgewood Pl getting on to Kensington Terr
frequently speed along the road especially after school near Colombia High School and is
used as a bypass for Valley St. There has been a stop sign request to be placed on
Kensington on the intersection of Kensington Terr and Edgewood Pl by the neighborhood
association but this is not recommended by the MUTCD 2001. This issue must be
looked at more closely along with the issues near Columbia High School.
Crash Data: 8 Reported Crash Incidents From Jan 1, 2001-Dec 31, 2004

CODE OF THE TOWNSHIP OF MAPLEWOOD, NEW JERSEY, v28, LUL, v13
Updated 8-15-2005
PART II GENERAL LEGISLATION
CHAPTER 271, ZONING AND DEVELOPMENT REGULATIONS
ARTICLE IV, Design and Performance Standards

§ 271-55. Sight triangles.

Sight triangles shall be required at each corner of an intersection of streets and at
intersections of streets and driveways serving commercial, industrial and multifamily
housing developments. Driveways shall be classified as a local street for purposes of
establishing distances. The area within sight triangles shall be either dedicated as part of
the street right-of-way or kept as part of the lot and identified as a sight triangle
easement. The standards set forth herein shall apply to all intersections in the Township,
regardless of whether an additional right-of-way is dedicated or an easement provided.
No grading, planting or structure shall be erected or maintained more than 24 inches
above the center-line grade of the intersecting street or driveway or lower than 10 feet
above their center lines, excluding street name signs and official traffic regulation signs.
Where any intersection involves earth banks or vegetation, including trees, the developer
shall trim or selectively thin trees and grade to provide the single triangle. The sight
triangle is that area bounded by the intersecting street lines and a straight line connecting
sight points located on each of the two intersecting street lines the following distances
from the point of intersection:

A.       Major streets at 100 feet; secondary streets at 60 feet; tertiary streets at 35 feet;
and local streets at 25 feet.
B.       Where the intersecting streets are both of a higher classification than local, two
overlapping sight triangles shall be required, formed by connecting the sight points noted
above with a sight point 25 feet on the intersecting street. The classification of existing
and proposed streets shall be those shown on the adopted Master Plan.
C.       Where streets or driveways intersect a state or county road, the sight triangle shall
conform to state or county requirements.
D.       A sight triangle easement shall be expressed on the plat as follows: "Sight triangle
easement subject to grading, planting and construction restrictions as provided in the
Maplewood Zoning and Development Regulations Ordinance."
E.       Portions of a lot set aside for the sight triangles may be calculated in determining
the lot area and minimum setbacks required by the zoning provisions.

   APPENDIX H


Traffic Signal Warrant
INTRODUCTION:

At the request of the Township of Maplewood, Keller and Kirkpatrick, Inc.
performed a preliminary traffic signal warrant analysis for the unsignalized
intersection of C.R. 638, Valley Street, and Jefferson Avenue. The intersection
of the two roadways occurs at milepost 1.23 of Valley Street. Valley Street and
Jefferson Avenue have a posted speed limit of 35 mph and 25 mph, respectively.
Limited intersection sight distance along with a steep grade along Jefferson
Avenue, which forms the stem of this `T' intersection, have been identified as
hazards to both motorists and pedestrians.

This study contains the results of the traffic signal warrant analysis for the
unsignalized intersection of Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue. The warrant
analysis has been performed in accordance with Chapter 4C of the Manual on
Uniform Traffic Control Devices, 2003 Edition (MUTCD), as amended by the
Federal Highway Administration.


DATA COLLECTION:

Keller and Kirkpatrick performed a classified manual turning movement count at
the intersection of Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue on Wednesday, October
18, 2006 between the hours of 6:00 A.M. and 6:00 P.M. The count data was
classified in 15-minute increments into the following three categories as per the
FHWA Traffic Monitoring Guide:

·   Pedestrians/Bicyclists
·   Automobiles/Light Trucks (Motorcycles, cars, SUV's, minivans, pick-up trucks
    and full-size vans, for personal or commercial use)
·   Medium Trucks (Single unit trucks)
·   Heavy Trucks/Buses (Tractor trailers)

Copies of the raw manual count data along with a flow diagram indicating the raw
volume for each movement and the intersection approach and exit leg totals
during the AM, midday and PM peak hours can be found in Appendix C.

Table 1 contains a summary of the existing major and minor street volumes for
the eight (8) highest hours as developed from the aforementioned count data. In
accordance with Section 4A.02 of the MUTCD, the major street and the minor
street are defined as those normally carrying the higher and lower volume of
vehicular traffic, respectively. Based on the intersection's traffic volumes, Valley
Street is the major street and Jefferson Avenue is the minor street.




Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue - Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis         Page 1
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
                            Table 1 ­ Existing Traffic Volumes

                      Major Street (Valley St.)       Minor Street (Jefferson Ave.)     Total

                     NB           SB       Total        EB         WB       Total      Volume

   7 - 8 AM          325         368        693          34            0      34         727
   8 ­ 9 AM          403         505        908          79            0      79         987

  12 ­ 1 PM          329         355        684          90            0      90         774
   1 ­ 2PM           341         401        742          77            0      77         819
   3 ­ 4 PM          423         486        909         131            0     131        1,040
   4 ­ 5 PM          472         541       1,031        113            0     113        1,126
   5 ­ 6 PM          536         577       1,113        132            0     132        1,245
                    3,169       3,568      6,737        722            0     722        7,459

WARRANT EVALUATION:

The MUTCD states that a signal warrant study should consider the effects of the
right turn vehicles from the minor street approaches and that engineering
judgment should be used to determine what, if any, portion of the right turn traffic
is subtracted from the minor street traffic count when evaluating the count
against the signal warrants. Since the minor street in this case is a single lane
with limited sight distance, no portion of the right turn traffic was subtracted from
the minor street traffic count for this analysis.

Section 4C.02 - Warrant 1, Eight-Hour Vehicular Volume: In order to satisfy
Warrant 1, the MUTCD provides a series of minimum traffic volume requirements
for both the major and minor streets for each of the highest eight hours
throughout the day with given conditions. The conditions are Condition A ­
Minimum Vehicular Volume and Condition B ­ Interruption of Continuous Traffic.
This warrant also specifies that if neither Condition A or B is met that a
combination of these conditions using 80 percent of the traffic volumes can be
used to satisfy the warrant. Table 2 summarizes the required traffic volumes to
satisfy Warrant 1 as per Table 4C-1 of the MUTCD. Table 3 summarizes the
existing traffic volumes for the highest eight hours and if they satisfy the
corresponding condition.

                Table 2: Warrant 1 - Traffic Volume Requirements
                                        Condition A           Condition B      Combination
             Volume
                                          (100%)                (100%)           (80%)
 Major Street (Both Approaches)             500                  750                  600
 Minor Street (One Direction)               150                  75                   120




Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue - Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis                   Page 2
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
                                                                      Table 3: Warrant 1 - Analysis

      Hour                                                  Major Street        Minor Street           Condition A            Condition B          Combination
                                                                                                                                                     A and B
    7 - 8 AM          693                                                               34                    No                      No                   No
    8 ­ 9 AM          908                                                               79                    No                      Yes                  No
   9 ­ 10 AM          675                                                               66                    No                      No                   No
 11 AM ­ 12 PM        684                                                               90                    No                      No                   No
    1 ­ 2PM           742                                                               77                    No                      No                   No
    3 ­ 4 PM          909                                                              131                    No                      Yes                  Yes
    4 ­ 5 PM         1,013                                                             113                    No                      Yes                  No
    5 ­ 6 PM         1,113                                                             132                    No                      Yes                  Yes
              Warrant Satisfied?                                                                              No                      No                   No

As indicated in Table 3, Warrant 1 is not satisfied.

Section 4C.03 - Warrant 2, Four-Hour Vehicular Volume: The MUTCD
specifies that Warrant 2 is satisfied when for each of any four hours of an
average day, the plotted points representing the vehicles per hour on the major
street (both approaches) and the corresponding vehicles per hour on the higher
volume minor street approach (one direction only) for the appropriate number of
lanes for both streets, all fall above the applicable curve in Figure 4C-1 of the
MUTCD. Figure 3 shows the plotted volume combination for the highest eight
hours throughout the day in comparison to the appropriate curve from Figure 4C-
2 of the MUTCD.
                         Figure 2 ­ Four Hour Warrant


                                                                    Warrant 2 - Peak Four-Hour Average Volume

          Minor Street High Volume Approach - VPH




                                                    300

                                                    200

                                                    150

                                                    100

                                                    50

                                                      100     200     300      400        500       600       700       800          900    1000    1100     1200
                                                                                     Major Street - Total of Both Approaches - VPH




                                                                    MUTCD Peak Four Hour Average Warrant         Observed




Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue - Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis                                                                                 Page 3
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
As indicated in Figure 2, Warrant 2 is not satisfied since only three of the highest
eight hours exceed the required curve.

Section 4C.04 - Warrant 3, Peak Hour: The MUTCD specifies that Warrant 3 is
intended for use at a location where traffic conditions are such that for a
minimum of one (1) hour of an average day, the minor street traffic suffers undue
delay when entering or crossing the major street. The MUTCD further states that
this warrant shall only be applied in unusual cases, such as office complexes,
manufacturing plants, industrial complexes, or high-occupancy vehicle facilities
that attract or discharge large numbers of vehicles over a short time. Therefore,
Warrant 3 is not applicable to this intersection.

Section 4C.05 - Warrant 4, Pedestrian Volume: The MUTCD specifies that
Warrant 4 is intended for application where the traffic volume on the major street
is so heavy that pedestrians experience excessive delay in crossing the major
street. The need for a traffic signal shall be considered under this warrant if both
of the following criteria are met:

A. The pedestrian volume crossing the major street during an average day is
   100 or more for each of any four hours or 190 or more during any one hour;
   and

B. There are fewer than 60 gaps per hour in the traffic stream of adequate length
   to allow pedestrians to cross during the same period when the pedestrian
   criterion is satisfied.

Based on field observation the pedestrian volumes crossing Valley Street at
Jefferson Avenue do not meet the criteria for Part A, above. Therefore, Warrant
4 is not satisfied.

Section 4C.06 - Warrant 5, School Crossing: The MUTCD specifies that
Warrant 5 is intended for application where the fact that school children cross the
major street is the principal reason to consider installing a traffic signal. Several
school children were observed crossing Valley Street at Jefferson Avenue during
the afternoon. However an established school crossing is located at the
intersection of Valley Street and Parker Avenue where the majority of school
children cross with the use of a school crossing guard. Therefore, Warrant 5 is
not satisfied at this location.

Section 4C.07 - Warrant 6, Coordinated Signal System: The MUTCD
specifies that Warrant 6 provides justification for the installation of a traffic signal
at an intersection to provide progressive movement in a coordinated signal
system where it would not otherwise be needed in order to maintain proper
platooning of vehicles. However, this warrant should not be applied where the
resultant spacing of traffic control signals would be less than 1,000 feet. Since
the nearest signal, located at Valley Street and Parker Avenue, is approximately

Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue - Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis            Page 4
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
573 feet from the intersection of Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue, Warrant 6 is
not satisfied.

Section 4C.08 - Warrant 7, Crash Experience: The MUTCD specifies that
Warrant 7 is intended for application where the severity and frequency of crashes
are the principal reasons to consider the installation of a traffic signal. The need
for a traffic signal shall be considered under this warrant if all of the following
criteria are met:

A. Adequate trial of alternatives with satisfactory observance and enforcement
   has failed to reduce the crash frequency, and:
B. Five or more reported crashes, of types susceptible to correction by a traffic
   signal, have occurred within a 12-month period, each crash involving personal
   injury or property damage apparently exceeding the applicable requirements
   for a reportable crash, and:
C. For each of any eight hours of an average day, the vehicles per hour (vph)
   given in both of the 80 percent columns of Condition A in Table 4C-1, or the
   vph in both of the 80 percent columns of Condition B in Table 4C-1 exists on
   the major street and the higher volume minor street approaches, respectively,
   to the intersection, or the volume of pedestrian traffic is not less than 80
   percent of the requirements specified in the Pedestrian Volume warrant.

According to the individual reports for crashes that occurred at the intersection of
Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue during the three-year period extending from
2004 to 2006 as provided by the Maplewood Township Engineering Department,
six, two and two crashes occurred during the years of 2004, 2005 and 2006,
respectively. It can be reasoned that a traffic signal could have prevented three
of the six crashes that occurred in 2004 and none of the other crashes during the
remaining years. In addition, an adequate trial and observance of other safety
measures has not been implemented and the existing vehicular and pedestrian
volumes do not satisfy the conditions of Part C, above. Therefore, Warrant 7 is
not satisfied since none of the criteria were met for crash experience.

Section 4C.09 - Warrant 8, Roadway Network: The MUTCD specifies that the
installation of a traffic signal may be justified to encourage concentration and
organization of traffic flow on a roadway network. Specifically, it states that the
intersection is to be common to two or more major routes. A major route as used
in this warrant shall have one or more of the following characteristics:

A. It is part of the street or highway system that serves as the principal roadway
   network for through traffic flow, or:
B. It includes rural or suburban highways outside, entering, or traversing a City,
   or:
C. It appears as a major route on an official plan, such as a major street plan in
   an urban area traffic and transportation study.



Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue - Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis         Page 5
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
Warrant 8 is not satisfied since none of the major route characteristics listed
above identify Jefferson Avenue as a major route.

CONCLUSION:

Based on our comprehensive engineering study of the traffic conditions,
pedestrian characteristics, and physical characteristics of the intersection of C.R.
638, Valley Street, and Jefferson Avenue, the installation of a traffic signal at this
intersection is not warranted based on the criteria established in Chapter 4C of
the MUTCD.




Valley Street and Jefferson Avenue - Traffic Signal Warrant Analysis          Page 6
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
    APPENDIX I


Multi-Way Stop Warrant
INTRODUCTION:

At the request of the Township of Maplewood, Essex County, Keller and
Kirkpatrick, Inc. performed a preliminary multi-way stop needs analysis for the
unsignalized intersection of Ridgewood Road and Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane.
Ridgewood Road and Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane form a four-legged intersection
with a stop condition along the approaches of Cedar Lane and E. Cedar Lane.
All roadways have a posted speed limit of 25 mph. Limited intersection sight
distance has been identified as a hazard by the Township of Maplewood along
with speeding along Ridgewood Road.

This study contains the results of the multi-way stop needs analysis for the
unsignalized intersection of Ridgewood Road and Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane.
The needs analysis has been performed in accordance with Chapter 2B of the
Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices, 2003 Edition (MUTCD), as amended
by the Federal Highway Administration.


DATA COLLECTION:

GPI performed a classified manual turning movement count at the intersection of
Ridgewood Road and Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane on Thursday, October 19, 2006
between the hours of 6:00 A.M. and 6:00 P.M. The count data was classified in
15-minute increments into the following three categories as per the FHWA Traffic
Monitoring Guide:

·   Pedestrians/Bicyclists
·   Automobiles/Light Trucks (Motorcycles, cars, SUV's, minivans, pick-up trucks
    and full-size vans, for personal or commercial use)
·   Medium Trucks (Single unit trucks)
·   Heavy Trucks/Buses (Tractor trailers)

Copies of the raw manual count data along with a flow diagram indicating the raw
volume for each movement and the intersection approach and exit leg totals
during the AM, midday and PM peak hours can be found in Appendix C.

Table 1 contains a summary of the existing major and minor street volumes for
the eight (8) highest hours as developed from the aforementioned count data. In
accordance with Section 4A.02 of the MUTCD, the major street and the minor
street are defined as those normally carrying the higher and lower volume of
vehicular traffic, respectively. Based on the intersection's traffic volumes,
Ridgewood Road is the major street and Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane is the minor
street.




Ridgewood Road & Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane ­ Multi-Way Stop Warrant Analysis   Page 1
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
                          Table 1 ­ Existing Traffic Volumes

                 Major Street (Ridgewood Rd.)      Minor Street (Cedar La.)     Total
    Hour
                   NB          SB      Total       EB        WB        Total   Volume

   7 - 8 AM        136         165      301         34        9          43     344
   8 ­ 9 AM        172         228      400         40        10         50     450
11 AM ­ 12 PM      101         109      210         22        3          25     235
  12 ­ 1 PM        144         109      253         24        4          28     281
   1 ­ 2PM         120         100      220         22        6          28     248

   4 ­ 5 PM        166         158      324         30        7          37     361
   5 ­ 6 PM        217         176      393         37        10         47     440
 TOTAL (8 hr)     1,250       1,235    2,485       251        56        307    2,792



EVALUATION:

A needs evaluation was conducted using the guidance presented in Part 2B.07
of the MUTCD.

Criterion A ­ Interim Measure Prior to Signalization: In accordance with the
MUTCD, in circumstances where traffic control signals are justified, a multi-way
stop installation may be used as an interim measure until arrangements can be
made for the installation of the traffic control signal.

Criterion A is not satisfied since the multi-way stop condition is not perceived to
be an interim measure for this intersection.

Criterion B ­ Crash Experience: The MUTCD states that the need for a multi-
way stop shall be considered if five or more reported crashes, of types
susceptible to correction by a multi-way stop installation, have occurred within a
12-month period. Such crashes include right- and left-turn collisions as well as
right-angle collisions.

According to the individual reports for crashes that occurred at the intersection of
Ridgewood Road and Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane during the three-year period
extending from 2004 to 2006 as provided by the Maplewood Township
Engineering Department, no reported crashes occurred during 2004 while two
reported crashes occurred during 2005 and then again in 2006. It can be
reasoned that a multi-way stop could have prevented the four total crashes that
occurred in 2005 and 2006. However, due to the insufficient number of
correctable crashes during a 12-month period, Criterion B is not satisfied.

Criterion C ­ Minimum Volumes: The MUTCD provides a series of minimum
traffic volume requirements for both the major and minor streets for each of the


Ridgewood Road & Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane ­ Multi-Way Stop Warrant Analysis    Page 2
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
highest eight hours throughout the day with given conditions. The conditions are
as follows:

1. The vehicular volume entering the intersection from the major street
   approaches (total of both approaches) averages at least 300 vehicles per
   hour for any 8 hours of an average day, and
2. The combined vehicular, pedestrian, and bicycle volume entering the
   intersection from the minor street approaches (total of both approaches)
   averages at least 200 units per hour for the same 8 hours, with an average
   delay to minor-street vehicular traffic of at least 30 seconds per vehicle during
   the highest hour, but
3. If the 85th-percentile approach speed of the major-street traffic exceeds 65
   km/h or exceeds 40 mph, the minimum vehicular volume warrants are 70
   percent of the above values.

As indicated in Table 2, Criterion C.1 is met, C.2 is not met and C.3 is not met
since the 85th percentile approach speed of the major street is less than 40 mph.
Therefore, Criterion C is not satisfied.

           Table 2: Multi-Way Stops - Traffic Volume Requirements
                                    Average 8 Hour
              Volume                                   Warrant (100%)    Warrant (80%)
                                    Volume (veh/hr)
 Major Street (Both Approaches)           311                300              240
 Minor Street (Both Approaches)            46                200              160
 Warrant Satisfied?                                          No               No

Criterion D ­ Combination of Criteria: Where no single criterion is satisfied, a
multi-way stop installation should be considered when Criteria B, C.1 and C.2 are
all satisfied to 80 percent of the minimum values. Since only Criterion C.1 is
satisfied to or greater than 80 percent, Criterion D is not satisfied.


CONCLUSION:

Based on our comprehensive engineering study of the traffic conditions,
pedestrian characteristics, and physical characteristics of the intersection of
Ridgewood Road and Cedar Avenue/E. Cedar Lane, the installation of a multi-
way stop at this intersection is not justified based on the criteria established in
Chapter 2B of the MUTCD.




Ridgewood Road & Cedar Lane/E. Cedar Lane ­ Multi-Way Stop Warrant Analysis     Page 3
Township of Maplewood, Essex County
